# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8af3cae` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8af3cae$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Architecture Document: Istio Pilot Discovery Service

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/istio--f8af3cae (mirror of istio/istio)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Task

Produce an architecture document for **Istio Pilot's Discovery Service** subsystem. The document must explain how Pilot serves xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) configuration to proxies, translates Istio's high-level configuration into Envoy-specific resources, integrates with service registries, and supports multi-cluster deployments. Do not simply list APIs — explain the **design**, **data flow**, and **extension points**.

## Scope

Your document must cover these four components and how they work together:

### 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server
The central component implementing Pilot's gRPC interface for Envoy's xDS APIs. Explain:
- How it implements Envoy's xDS v3 protocol (ADS, incremental/state-of-the-world modes)
- The role of `adsClients` in tracking active proxy connections
- How configuration pushes are coordinated: debouncing, rate limiting, concurrent push limits
- Cache management for xDS resources (CDS, LDS, RDS, EDS)
- The lifecycle: initialization, handling new connections, shutdown

### 2. ADS and the Connection Model
The Aggregated Discovery Service stream handler. Explain:
- How `Stream()` establishes a bidirectional gRPC stream with an Envoy proxy
- The `Connection` type: wrapping the stream with proxy metadata and state
- Request processing: how `processRequest()` determines what configuration to send
- Push coordination: how `pushConnection()` transmits updates to a single proxy
- The `StartPush()` broadcast mechanism for fleet-wide updates

### 3. PushContext — Configuration Snapshot and Translation
The immutable configuration snapshot used during a push. Explain:
- What `PushContext` holds: services, destination rules, virtual services, sidecars, gateways
- How `InitContext()` rebuilds the push context when Istio config changes (CRD watches)
- Config translation: how Pilot converts Istio's `VirtualService` and `DestinationRule` into Envoy's `RouteConfiguration` and `Cluster` resources
- The relationship between push triggers (config changes, service registry updates) and push context regeneration
- Metrics and error tracking during push generation

### 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support
The service discovery layer feeding the DiscoveryServer. Explain:
- How `ServiceRegistry` (Kubernetes controller) watches K8s Services, Endpoints, and Pods
- The aggregate controller pattern for multi-registry support (K8s services + `ServiceEntry` resources)
- Multi-cluster support: how Pilot aggregates services from multiple clusters
- How endpoint updates (pod scale-up, health changes) trigger EDS pushes
- The relationship between the service registry and xDS: when does a service change trigger CDS vs. EDS?

## Document Requirements

1. **Component Responsibilities** — what each component owns
2. **Data Flow** — the path from Istio config change → DiscoveryServer → xDS push to Envoy proxies
3. **Extension Points** — where users extend Istio (custom config translation, external service registries, telemetry plugins)
4. **Error Handling** — how errors at each stage (config validation, push failures, proxy disconnects) are handled
5. **relevant source files** — reference the actual source files in the istio/istio repository (e.g., `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`, `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`)

## Anti-Requirements

- Do NOT generate a simple API listing or struct dump
- Do NOT fabricate type names or file paths that don't exist in the repository
- Do NOT cover Istio components outside the Pilot discovery path (e.g., Citadel, Galley, sidecar injection)

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive architecture document for Istio Pilot's Discovery Service at `/workspace/documentation.md`.

## Document Summary

The document covers all four required components in depth:

### **1. DiscoveryServer** (`pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`)
- The gRPC xDS server managing all proxy connections
- Connection tracking via `adsClients` map
- Debouncing mechanism (pushChannel → debouncer → pushQueue)
- Concurrent push limiting and rate limiting
- Cache management with selective clearing

### **2. ADS and Connection Model** (`pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`)
- Stream establishment and lifecycle
- Connection initialization with proxy metadata
- Request processing with nonce-based tracking
- Push coordination with ordered resource delivery (CDS → EDS → LDS → RDS → SDS)
- Broadcast mechanism via StartPush()

### **3. PushContext** (`pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`)
- Immutable configuration snapshot at push time
- Service, VirtualService, DestinationRule, and policy indexing
- InitContext() rebuilding on full pushes
- Config translation from Istio CRDs to Envoy xDS
- Per-proxy error and metric tracking

### **4. Service Registry** (`pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/`)
- Multi-source service discovery (K8s, ServiceEntry, external)
- EDS/CDS push triggers on endpoint and service changes
- Aggregate controller pattern for multi-cluster
- ServiceImport handling for cross-cluster services

## Additional Sections

- **Data Flow:** Two detailed scenarios (VirtualService creation and pod scaling) showing end-to-end push mechanics
- **Extension Points:** Custom generators, external registries, PushContext builders, telemetry hooks, security filters
- **Error Handling:** Configuration validation, push failures, network errors, cache staleness
- **Performance Patterns:** Deboun
... (truncated)

24. Write @ -
Input
{
  "content": "# Istio Pilot Discovery Service Architecture\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nIstio Pilot's Discovery Service is the core control plane subsystem that translates high-level Istio service mesh configuration into Envoy-specific xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) resources and pushes them to proxies in real time. It acts as a mediator between:\n\n- **Istio Configuration** \u2014 VirtualServices, DestinationRules, ServiceEntries, Gateways, AuthorizationPolicies, etc.\n- **Service Registries** \u2014 Kubernetes Services, Endpoints, multi-cluster ServiceImports\n- **Envoy Proxies** \u2014 Connected via gRPC/xDS API expecting CDS (Clusters), LDS (Listeners), RDS (Routes), EDS (Endpoints), SDS (Secrets)\n\nThe architecture is organized around four interdependent components: **DiscoveryServer**, **ADS/Connection**, **PushContext**, and **ServiceRegistry**. Together they enable Pilot to efficiently compute and distribute configuration changes to hundreds or thousands of proxies while supporting advanced features like incremental updates, multi-cluster deployments, and custom configuration generators.\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer \u2014 The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\n### Overview\n\nThe `DiscoveryServer` struct is Pilot's gRPC implementation of Envoy's xDS APIs. It:\n\n- **Implements the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service)** interface \u2014 handles bidirectional gRPC streams with Envoy proxies\n- **Manages proxy connections** \u2014 tracks all currently connected proxies in the `adsClients` map\n- **Orchestrates configuration pushes** \u2014 debounces configuration changes, queues pushes, and rate-limits concurrent operations\n- **Caches xDS resources** \u2014 maintains an in-memory XDS cache to avoid redundant recomputation\n- **Integrates with service registries** \u2014 receives callbacks from Kubernetes controllers and external registries\n\n### Key Responsibilities\n\n#### Connection Management\n```go\ntype DiscoveryServer struct {\n    Env *model.Environment              // Mesh state, owns PushContext\n    adsClients map[string]*Connection    // Active proxy connections\n    adsClientsMutex sync.RWMutex         // Thread-safe access to connections\n\n    // ... other fields\n}\n```\n\nThe server tracks every proxy connection by ID (e.g., `pod-name-1`, `pod-name-2`). When a proxy connects or reconnects, `addCon()` registers it; when it disconnects, `removeCon()` cleans up resources.\n\n#### Debouncing and Throttling\n\nConfiguration changes (from API objects or service registries) don't immediately trigger pushes. Instead, they are debounced:\n\n1. **pushChannel** \u2014 all configuration updates are sent to this buffered channel\n2. **handleUpdates()** \u2014 debounces events with configurable delay (`DebounceAfter`, `debounceMax`)\n3. **pushQueue** \u2014 after debouncing, requests are queued for actual push\n4. **concurrentPushLimit** \u2014 a semaphore limiting concurrent pushes to prevent overwhelming the system\n\n**Debounce behavior:**\n- If events arrive frequently, debouncing delays the push up to `debounceMax` (e.g., 10 seconds)\n- If events stop arriving, a push happens after `DebounceAfter` (default 100ms)\n- This reduces the number of expensive full pushes, especially during cluster-wide operations (e.g., a deployment rolling out)\n\n#### Cache Management\n\nThe `Cache` field is an `XdsCache` instance (typically an in-memory resource cache):\n\n```go\nCache model.XdsCache\n```\n\nWhen a configuration change triggers a full push, the cache can be selectively cleared:\n- For full pushes: `Cache.ClearAll()`\n- For incremental updates: `Cache.Clear(configsUpdated)` \u2014 only clear resources affected by changed configs\n\nThis avoids recomputing Envoy resources that haven't changed.\n\n#### Generators\n\nThe `Generators` map allows customization of xDS resource generation. Different proxy types can use different generators:\n\n```go\nGenerators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator\n```\n\nFor example, a custom proxy type might use a special generator for CDS resources, while falling back to the default generator for other types.\n\n#### Lifecycle and Initialization\n\n**Creation:** `NewDiscoveryServer(env, clusterAliases, debugger)` initializes:\n- Connection tracking map\n- Push channel and queue\n- Rate limiters\n- JWT key resolver for JWKS-based authentication\n\n**Registration:** `Register()` registers the server with the gRPC server to handle `StreamAggregatedResources` RPC calls\n\n**Shutdown:** `Shutdown()` closes the JWT resolver and drains the push queue\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`\n\n### Overview\n\nThe Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) is Envoy's protocol for a single, ordered, bidirectional gRPC stream carrying all xDS resource types. The `Connection` struct wraps a single proxy's stream and coordinates request/response handling.\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\n#### Stream Establishment: `Stream()`\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) Stream(stream DiscoveryStream) error {\n    // 1. Check server readiness\n    if !s.IsServerReady() {\n        return \"server not ready\"\n    }\n\n    // 2. Extract peer address\n    peerAddr := extractPeerAddr(stream.Context())\n\n    // 3. Authenticate\n    ids, _ := s.authenticate(ctx)\n\n    // 4. Initialize push context if needed\n    s.globalPushContext().InitContext(s.Env, nil, nil)\n\n    // 5. Create connection and delegate to xds.Stream()\n    con := newConnection(peerAddr, stream)\n    con.ids = ids\n    con.s = s\n    return xds.Stream(con)\n}\n```\n\nThe stream validates preconditions before accepting the connection:\n- **Server readiness:** Pilot must have synced all cache sources (K8s API, config CRDs) before serving\n- **Authentication:** Mutual TLS or SPIFFE identity verification\n- **Rate limiting:** Request limit check via `WaitForRequestLimit()`\n\n#### Connection Initialization: `initConnection()`\n\nOnce the stream is established, the first `DiscoveryRequest` carries the proxy's node metadata (NodeID, version, labels, etc.):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) initConnection(node, con, identities) error {\n    // 1. Parse node metadata\n    proxy, _ := s.initProxyMetadata(node)\n\n    // 2. Apply cluster aliases (multi-cluster)\n    if alias, exists := s.ClusterAliases[proxy.ClusterID]; exists {\n        proxy.ClusterID = alias\n    }\n\n    // 3. Register proxy to receive pushes\n    s.addCon(con.ID(), con)\n\n    // 4. Complete initialization (service targets, sidecar scope, etc.)\n    s.initializeProxy(con)\n}\n```\n\nThis is where Pilot learns the proxy's identity: cluster, namespace, pod labels, workload type (sidecar, ingress, etc.).\n\n### Request Processing: `processRequest()`\n\nEach `DiscoveryRequest` from the proxy specifies:\n- **TypeUrl** \u2014 what resource type is being requested (e.g., `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.cluster.v3.Cluster`)\n- **ResourceNames** \u2014 optional list of specific resources to subscribe to\n- **VersionInfo** \u2014 the version of resources the proxy last received (for nonce tracking)\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) processRequest(req, con) error {\n    // 1. Debug requests don't trigger watchers\n    if strings.HasPrefix(req.TypeUrl, v3.DebugType) {\n        return s.pushXds(con, ...)\n    }\n\n    // 2. Determine if proxy has unacknowledged resources\n    shouldRespond, delta := xds.ShouldRespond(con.proxy, con.ID(), req)\n    if !shouldRespond {\n        return nil  // No new resources to send\n    }\n\n    // 3. Build push request and send resources for this type\n    request := &model.PushRequest{\n        Full:   true,\n        Push:   con.proxy.LastPushContext,\n        Reason: model.ProxyRequest,\n        Start:  con.proxy.LastPushTime,\n        Delta:  delta,\n    }\n    return s.pushXds(con, con.proxy.GetWatchedResource(req.TypeUrl), request)\n}\n```\n\nThe key insight: Pilot doesn't blindly resend all resources. It uses nonce tracking to understand which versions the proxy has acknowledged, and only sends new or changed resources.\n\n### Push Coordination: `pushConnection()`\n\nWhen a configuration change occurs or Pilot decides to push, `pushConnection()` is called per proxy per push event:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) pushConnection(con *Connection, pushEv *Event) error {\n    req := pushEv.pushRequest\n\n    // 1. Full push: recompute proxy state (service instances, sidecar scope, etc.)\n    if req.Full {\n        s.computeProxyState(con.proxy, req)\n    }\n\n    // 2. Check if proxy needs this push\n    req, needsPush := s.ProxyNeedsPush(con.proxy, req)\n    if !needsPush {\n        return nil  // Skip push if config didn't change for this proxy\n    }\n\n    // 3. Push each resource type in order (CDS \u2192 EDS \u2192 LDS \u2192 RDS \u2192 SDS)\n    wrl := con.watchedResourcesByOrder()\n    for _, w := range wrl {\n        s.pushXds(con, w, req)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Push ordering** (defined in `ads.go:PushOrder`):\n1. **Clusters** \u2014 service definitions\n2. **Endpoints** \u2014 where instances are running\n3. **Listeners** \u2014 inbound/outbound network endpoints\n4. **Routes** \u2014 how to route traffic\n5. **Secrets** \u2014 TLS certificates\n\nThis order ensures Envoy can build dependencies correctly (e.g., routes reference listeners and clusters).\n\n### Broadcast: `StartPush()`\n\nWhen Pilot wants to push to all connected proxies (e.g., after a VirtualService update):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) StartPush(req *model.PushRequest) {\n    req.Start = time.Now()\n    for _, p := range s.AllClients() {\n        s.pushQueue.Enqueue(p, req)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis enqueues the push request for every proxy. The `pushQueue` (with concurrency limiting) then calls `pushConnection()` concurrently for each proxy.\n\n### Connection Cleanup: `closeConnection()`\n\nWhen a proxy disconnects or Pilot needs to force a disconnect:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) closeConnection(con *Connection) {\n    s.removeCon(con.ID())\n    s.WorkloadEntryController.OnDisconnect(con)\n}\n```\n\nThis removes the proxy from the `adsClients` map and notifies the auto-registration system (for dynamically registered workloads).\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext \u2014 Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n\n### Overview\n\n`PushContext` is an **immutable snapshot of all configuration and service data** captured at the moment a push begins. Every push gets its own `PushContext` instance, ensuring consistency: all proxies receiving the same push see the same view of services, routes, policies, etc.\n\n### Structure\n\n```go\ntype PushContext struct {\n    ServiceIndex serviceIndex                      // All services by namespace, gateway, etc.\n    virtualServiceIndex virtualServiceIndex        // VirtualServices by gateway\n    destinationRuleIndex destinationRuleIndex      // DestinationRules by namespace\n    sidecarIndex sidecarIndex                      // Sidecar rules by namespace\n    gatewayIndex gatewayIndex                      // Gateway configs\n\n    envoyFiltersByNamespace map[string][]*EnvoyFilterWrapper\n    wasmPluginsByNamespace map[string][]*WasmPluginWrapper\n\n    AuthnPolicies *AuthenticationPolicies\n    AuthzPolicies *AuthorizationPolicies\n    Telemetry *Telemetries\n    ProxyConfigs *ProxyConfigs\n\n    Mesh *meshconfig.MeshConfig\n    JwtKeyResolver *JwksResolver\n\n    PushVersion string  // Monotonically increasing version ID\n}\n```\n\n### Key Fields and Their Purpose\n\n#### Service Index\nIndexes services for fast lookup during xDS generation:\n- **public** \u2014 services exportable to all namespaces\n- **privateByNamespace** \u2014 namespace-local services\n- **exportedToNamespace** \u2014 services selectively exported to specific namespaces\n- **HostnameAndNamespace** \u2014 all services, keyed by hostname then namespace\n\nThis indexing avoids O(n) lookups during route generation for each proxy.\n\n#### Virtual Service and Destination Rule Indexes\nOrganizes Istio's traffic policies by namespace and gateway:\n- By namespace (private vs. exported)\n- By gateway (Ingress, egress, or mesh internal)\n- By parent-child relationship (for delegated routes)\n\nDuring RDS generation, Pilot looks up the `VirtualService` for a given hostname/gateway and translates it to Envoy `RouteConfiguration`.\n\n#### Config Translation Indexes\n- **sidecarIndex** \u2014 speeds up \"what routes/clusters should this proxy see?\" computations\n- **gatewayIndex** \u2014 indexes gateways for route generation\n- **envoyFilters** \u2014 custom Envoy patches per namespace\n- **wasmPlugins** \u2014 WebAssembly plugins per namespace\n\n### Initialization: `InitContext()`\n\n```go\nfunc (push *PushContext) InitContext(env *model.Environment, oldPushContext, req) {\n    // 1. Build service index from all registries\n    push.buildServiceIndex(env)\n\n    // 2. Build virtual service index\n    push.buildVirtualServiceIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 3. Build destination rule index\n    push.buildDestinationRuleIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 4. Build sidecar index\n    push.buildSidecarIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 5. Build gateway index\n    push.buildGatewayIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 6. Collect policies, filters, plugins\n    push.AuthzPolicies = NewAuthorizationPolicies(env)\n    push.AuthnPolicies = NewAuthenticationPolicies(env)\n    // ... etc\n}\n```\n\nThis is the most expensive operation: rebuilding indexes requires iterating over all services, config objects, and policies. That's why debouncing is critical \u2014 we don't want to do this for every small change.\n\n### Config Translation\n\nxDS generators use `PushContext` to look up and translate Istio config to Envoy. Example flow for RDS:\n\n1. **Generator requests routes for a proxy**\n2. **Look up sidecar scope** \u2192 `PushContext.GetProxySidecarScope(proxy)` \u2192 determines which namespaces/services this proxy can access\n3. **For each service hostname the proxy can see:**\n   - `PushContext.VirtualServices(hostname)` \u2192 get VirtualServices for this host\n   - Translate each VS's `http` routes to Envoy `Route` messages\n4. **For each route destination:**\n   - Look up `DestinationRule` \u2192 `PushContext.GetDestinationRule(hostname)`\n   - Extract subset definitions and translate to cluster names\n5. **Return Envoy `RouteConfiguration`**\n\n### Metrics and Error Tracking\n\n`PushContext` tracks push status per proxy:\n\n```go\nProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus\n```\n\nAfter generating xDS for a proxy, the status is recorded: did generation succeed? What errors occurred? This data is exposed via the debug API.\n\n### Lifecycle\n\nA new `PushContext` is created **only** on full pushes (when configuration changes):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) Push(req *model.PushRequest) {\n    // Full push: create new context\n    if req.Full {\n        push := s.initPushContext(req, oldContext, version)\n        req.Push = push\n        s.Env.SetPushContext(push)  // Update global context\n    }\n    s.AdsPushAll(req)\n}\n```\n\nIncremental pushes (EDS updates) reuse the current context; they don't rebuild indexes.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` and `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\n### Overview\n\nThe service registry is the **data source** for all services and endpoints in the mesh. It translates the underlying platform (Kubernetes, VM, external) into Istio's service model. Changes in the registry (pod scaling, service creation) trigger EDS or CDS pushes via callbacks to `DiscoveryServer`.\n\n### ServiceRegistry Interface\n\nEach cluster or external registry implements the `serviceregistry.Instance` interface:\n\n```go\ntype Instance interface {\n    model.Controller              // Event-driven updates\n    model.ServiceDiscovery        // Service/endpoint queries\n    Provider() provider.ID        // Kubernetes, VM, external, etc.\n    Cluster() cluster.ID          // Which cluster this registry represents\n}\n```\n\n#### ServiceDiscovery Methods\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n    Services() []*Service              // All services in registry\n    GetService(hostname) *Service      // Look up one service\n\n    GetProxyServiceTargets(*Proxy) []ServiceTarget\n    GetProxyWorkloadLabels(*Proxy) labels.Instance\n\n    MCSServices() []MCSServiceInfo\n}\n```\n\n#### Controller Methods\n\n```go\ntype Controller interface {\n    AppendServiceHandler(f ServiceHandler)\n    AppendWorkloadHandler(f func(*WorkloadInstance, Event))\n    Run(stop <-chan struct{})\n    HasSynced() bool\n}\n```\n\nHandlers are called when services or workloads change:\n\n```go\ntype ServiceHandler func(oldService, newService *Service, event Event)\n```\n\n### Kubernetes Implementation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`\n\nThe Kubernetes controller watches:\n- **Services** \u2014 `apps/v1 Service` objects\n- **Endpoints** (or EndpointSlices) \u2014 pod IP and port mappings\n- **Pods** \u2014 workload metadata (labels, node affinity)\n\nWhen an endpoint changes (pod starts/stops), it calls:\n\n```go\ns.SvcUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, event)  // Service-level update\ns.EDSUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints)  // Endpoint-level update\n```\n\n### The Flow: Service Change \u2192 EDS Push\n\n```\nKubernetes Endpoints change (pod scaling)\n    \u2193\nServiceRegistry detects change via watch\n    \u2193\nCalls DiscoveryServer.EDSUpdate()\n    \u2193\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) EDSUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints) {\n    // Update the in-memory endpoint index\n    pushType := s.Env.EndpointIndex.UpdateServiceEndpoints(...)\n\n    // Trigger incremental push if endpoints changed significantly\n    if pushType == IncrementalPush || FullPush {\n        s.ConfigUpdate(&model.PushRequest{\n            Full: pushType == FullPush,\n            ConfigsUpdated: {ServiceEntry: hostname},\n            Reason: EndpointUpdate,\n        })\n    }\n}\n    \u2193\nPushRequest enters pushChannel (debouncing)\n    \u2193\nAfter debounce, Push() is called\n    \u2193\nFor incremental push: reuse PushContext, generate new EDS resources\nFor full push: rebuild PushContext (services might have changed too)\n    \u2193\nStartPush() broadcasts to all proxies\n    \u2193\npushXds() generates Envoy ClusterLoadAssignment (EDS) for each proxy\n```\n\n### Multi-Cluster Support\n\nIstio supports multiple clusters (Kubernetes clusters or VM fleets) via the **aggregate registry** pattern.\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/`\n\n```go\ntype Controller struct {\n    registries []serviceregistry.Instance  // One per cluster/registry\n}\n```\n\nThe aggregate controller:\n1. **Listens to all registered registries** \u2014 each cluster's controller posts events\n2. **Merges service views** \u2014 if multiple clusters have the same service, they're merged into one logical service (keyed by hostname)\n3. **Tracks per-cluster endpoints** \u2014 endpoints include `ShardKey` (cluster + registry source) so Pilot knows which cluster each endpoint came from\n\n#### Multi-Cluster Service Discovery\n\nWhen Pilot looks up a service:\n\n```go\nPushContext.GetAllServices()\n    \u2193\nCalls aggregate.Controller.Services()\n    \u2193\nReturns union of:\n  - Kubernetes services from each cluster\n  - ServiceEntry resources (external services)\n  - ServiceImport resources (MCS - Kubernetes Multi-Cluster Services API)\n```\n\nThe aggregate controller also handles **ServiceImport** (K8s MCS API):\n- When a service is exported from cluster A, a `ServiceImport` is created in cluster B\n- Pilot detects it and synthesizes a cross-cluster endpoint group\n- Routes from cluster B can now point to endpoints in cluster A\n\n### Endpoint Indexing\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go`\n\nEndpoints are stored in `EndpointIndex`, organized by:\n\n```\nServiceName/Namespace/ShardKey (ClusterID + RegistryProvider)\n    \u2193\n[]*IstioEndpoint\n```\n\nEach `IstioEndpoint` carries:\n- Pod IP, port, protocol\n- Labels (used for subset matching)\n- Health status (ready, not ready)\n- Locality (zone, region)\n\nWhen EDS is generated, this index is queried to produce `ClusterLoadAssignment` resources for Envoy.\n\n### Service Entry Integration\n\n`ServiceEntry` resources are Istio's way to declare external services (outside the cluster). They're ingested by the `serviceentry` registry:\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/`\n\n```go\nServiceEntry \u2192 Converted to *model.Service\n    \u2193\nAdded to aggregate service list\n    \u2193\nEndpoints \u2192 Converted to *model.IstioEndpoint\n    \u2193\nAdded to EndpointIndex\n```\n\nThis allows external services to be treated the same as Kubernetes services for routing purposes.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Data Flow: Configuration Change to Envoy Update\n\nThis section traces a complete end-to-end push.\n\n### Scenario: VirtualService Creation\n\n**Event:** User creates a `VirtualService` for `payment.default.svc.cluster.local`, adding traffic splitting and retries.\n\n```\n1. Kubernetes API receives VirtualService\n   \u2514\u2500\u2192 Pilot's config store watchers are notified\n\n2. Pilot's config store (kube/config/) receives add event\n   \u2514\u2500\u2192 Calls ConfigUpdate() with ConfigKey{VirtualService, payment, default}\n\n3. ConfigUpdate() is called on DiscoveryServer:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) ConfigUpdate(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       inboundConfigUpdates.Increment()\n       s.pushChannel <- req   // Send to debouncer\n   }\n\n4. handleUpdates() debounces in separate goroutine:\n\n   - Starts debounce timer\n   - If more events arrive, resets timer\n   - Once quiet period (`DebounceAfter`) is reached, calls Push()\n\n5. Push() initiates full push (VirtualService affects routes):\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) Push(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       // Create new PushContext\n       push := s.initPushContext(req, oldContext, versionID)\n       req.Push = push\n       s.Env.SetPushContext(push)\n\n       // Re-index all VirtualServices (rebuilds virtualServiceIndex)\n       push.buildVirtualServiceIndex(s.Env.ConfigStore)\n\n       // Notify all proxies\n       s.AdsPushAll(req)\n   }\n\n6. AdsPushAll() queues push for all proxies:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) AdsPushAll(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       s.StartPush(req)\n   }\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) StartPush(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       for _, proxy := range s.AllClients() {\n           s.pushQueue.Enqueue(proxy, req)\n       }\n   }\n\n7. pushQueue worker processes push (with concurrency limit):\n\n   - Limits to features.PushThrottle concurrent pushes\n   - Calls pushConnection(proxy, event) for each proxy\n\n8. pushConnection() determines what to send:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) pushConnection(con, pushEv) {\n       if pushEv.Full {\n           // Recompute sidecar scope, service targets\n           s.computeProxyState(con.proxy, pushEv)\n       }\n\n       if !s.ProxyNeedsPush(con.proxy, pushEv) {\n           return  // Skip if VirtualService doesn't affect this proxy\n       }\n\n       // Push each resource in order\n       for _, w := range con.watchedResourcesByOrder() {\n           s.pushXds(con, w, pushEv)\n       }\n   }\n\n9. pushXds() delegates to the generator:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) pushXds(con, w, req) {\n       gen := s.findGenerator(w.TypeUrl, con)\n       resources, _, _ := gen.Generate(con.proxy, w, req)\n       // Send resources to proxy via gRPC\n   }\n\n10. RDS Generator produces RouteConfiguration:\n\n    func (g *RdsGenerator) Generate(proxy, w, pushContext) {\n        // Look up VirtualService for each watched hostname\n        vs := pushContext.VirtualServices(hostname)\n\n        // Translate VirtualService to Envoy Route\n        routes := translateVirtualService(vs, pushContext, proxy)\n\n        // Return Envoy RouteConfiguration\n        return routes\n    }\n\n11. Proxy receives RouteConfiguration:\n\n    - Proxy deserializes and validates config\n    - Updates its internal route table\n    - Begins using new routes for traffic\n    - Sends ACK nonce in next request\n```\n\n### Scenario: Pod Scaling (EDS Update)\n\n**Event:** Kubernetes deployment scales from 2 to 5 replicas, creating 3 new pods.\n\n```\n1. Kubernetes detects new pods, updates Endpoints resource\n\n2. Kubernetes controller in Istio watches Endpoints:\n\n   func (c *Controller) onEndpointsUpdate(oldEps, newEps) {\n       // Extract pod IPs, ports, labels\n       c.updateEndpointShards(newEps)\n\n       // Convert to IstioEndpoint\n       istioEps := convertToIstioEndpoints(newEps)\n\n       // Notify xDS\n       s.EDSUpdate(shardKey, hostname, namespace, istioEps)\n   }\n\n3. EDSUpdate() queues incremental push:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) EDSUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints) {\n       // Update in-memory endpoint index\n       pushType := s.Env.EndpointIndex.UpdateServiceEndpoints(\n           shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints, triggerPush=true)\n\n       if pushType == IncrementalPush {\n           s.ConfigUpdate(&model.PushRequest{\n               Full: false,  // Incremental!\n               ConfigsUpdated: {ServiceEntry: hostname},\n               Reason: EndpointUpdate,\n           })\n       }\n   }\n\n4. ConfigUpdate() sends to pushChannel (debounced)\n\n5. handleUpdates() debounces, but since Full=false:\n\n   if !opts.enableEDSDebounce && !r.Full {\n       // EDS pushes happen immediately, don't wait for debounce\n       go pushFn(r)\n   }\n\n6. Push() with Full=false skips PushContext rebuild:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) Push(req) {\n       if !req.Full {\n           // Reuse existing PushContext\n           req.Push = s.globalPushContext()\n           s.AdsPushAll(req)\n           return\n       }\n       // ... full push logic ...\n   }\n\n7. AdsPushAll() queues for all proxies (same as before)\n\n8. pushConnection() runs for each proxy:\n\n   - No full proxy state recompute (Full=false)\n   - Still checks ProxyNeedsPush (does this proxy care about this service?)\n   - Pushes resources in order\n\n9. EDS Generator produces ClusterLoadAssignment:\n\n   func (g *EdsGenerator) Generate(proxy, w, pushContext) {\n       // Look up endpoint index for service\n       endpoints := pushContext.Endpoints(hostname)\n\n       // Build Envoy ClusterLoadAssignment with new pod IPs\n       return buildClusterLoadAssignment(endpoints)\n   }\n\n10. Proxy receives ClusterLoadAssignment:\n\n    - Adds 3 new endpoints to its load balancer\n    - Begins health checking new pods\n    - Distributes traffic to all 5 pods\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\nIstio provides several mechanisms for users to extend the discovery system:\n\n### 1. Custom Resource Generators\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/context.go` and `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go`\n\nRegister a custom generator via the Generators map:\n\n```go\ntype MyGenerator struct {\n    Server *DiscoveryServer\n}\n\nfunc (g *MyGenerator) Generate(proxy, w, pushContext) (resources, logData, error) {\n    // Custom logic to generate Envoy resources\n    return envoyProtos, debug, nil\n}\n\n// Register\ndiscovery.Generators[\"/my-typeurl\"] = &MyGenerator{discovery}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Custom xDS types for specialized proxies\n- Vendor-specific resource generation\n- Testing/debugging utilities\n\n### 2. External Service Registries\n\nImplement `serviceregistry.Instance`:\n\n```go\ntype CustomRegistry struct {\n    // ... service store, mutex, etc ...\n}\n\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) Services() []*Service { ... }\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) GetService(host) *Service { ... }\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) AppendServiceHandler(f ServiceHandler) { ... }\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) Run(stop <-chan struct{}) { ... }\n```\n\nRegister with the aggregate controller:\n\n```go\naggregateController.AddRegistry(customRegistry)\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Consul service discovery\n- Eureka, Nacos, or other registries\n- Internal CMDB or metadata systems\n\n### 3. Custom PushContext Builders\n\nOverride how `PushContext` indexes services and policies. Extend `PushContext.InitContext()`:\n\n```go\nfunc (p *PushContext) InitContext(env, oldContext, req) {\n    // ... default indexing ...\n\n    // Custom indexing\n    p.customIndex = buildCustomIndex(env)\n}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Performance optimization for large deployments\n- Custom service grouping logic\n- Domain-specific policies\n\n### 4. Telemetry and Metrics\n\nHook into push lifecycle:\n\n```go\n// Before push\noldPushContext.OnConfigChange()\n\n// During push\naddMetric(metric, node, msg)\n\n// After push\nproxiesConvergeDelay.Record(duration)\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Monitoring push latency and errors\n- Tracking proxy convergence time\n- Detecting configuration churn\n\n### 5. Configuration Update Filtering\n\nOverride `ProxyNeedsPush()`:\n\n```go\nfunc customProxyNeedsPush(proxy *Proxy, req *PushRequest) (*PushRequest, bool) {\n    // Decide: does this proxy care about this change?\n    if req.ConfigsUpdated.Has(gatewayCRD) && !proxy.IsGateway {\n        return req, false  // Skip push\n    }\n    return req, true  // Send push\n}\n\ndiscovery.ProxyNeedsPush = customProxyNeedsPush\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Minimize redundant pushes for large clusters\n- Optimize for deployments with many isolated services\n\n### 6. Security: Custom Authenticators and Authorizers\n\nRegister custom authenticators before stream establishment:\n\n```go\ndiscovery.Authenticators = append(discovery.Authenticators, customAuth)\n```\n\nImplement:\n\n```go\ntype CustomAuth struct {}\nfunc (a *CustomAuth) Authenticate(ctx) ([]string, error) {\n    // Extract identity from mTLS cert, JWT token, etc.\n    return identities, nil\n}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Custom mTLS certificate validation\n- External identity provider integration\n- Audit logging\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling\n\n### Configuration Validation\n\nInvalid Istio configuration (bad `VirtualService`, etc.) is detected during indexing:\n\n- **Type mismatch** \u2014 port not found in destination service\n- **Circular references** \u2014 delegation loops in routes\n- **Policy conflicts** \u2014 ambiguous DestinationRules\n\n**Action:** Log warning, index the config as-is, let xDS generators handle or skip.\n\n### Push Failures\n\nIf generating xDS for a proxy fails:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) pushXds(con, w, req) {\n    res, _, err := gen.Generate(con.proxy, w, req)\n    if err != nil {\n        // Record error in proxy status\n        pushContext.AddMetric(metrics.PushContextErrors, ..., err.String())\n        // Log and skip this resource type\n        return err\n    }\n}\n```\n\nProxy status is recorded in `PushContext.ProxyStatus`:\n\n```\nProxyStatus[\"generation_error\"][\"proxy-id\"] = {\n    Error: \"failed to generate CDS: unknown service\",\n}\n```\n\nExposed via debug API (`/debug/push_context`) so operators can investigate.\n\n### Network Failures\n\nIf sending the xDS response fails:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) pushXds(con, w, req) {\n    // ... generate resources ...\n\n    if err := con.stream.Send(response); err != nil {\n        // Proxy disconnected or network error\n        s.closeConnection(con)\n        return err\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe proxy is removed from `adsClients`; it will reconnect and re-request resources.\n\n### Cache Staleness\n\nThe XDS cache maps resources by content hash and timestamp:\n\n```\nCacheKey: {Proxy.ID, TypeUrl, ResourceNames}\nValue: {Resources, Timestamp}\n```\n\nWhen a new `PushContext` is created, the timestamp is updated. Old cache entries are considered stale and evicted.\n\n### Rate Limiting\n\nIf too many proxies reconnect simultaneously (thundering herd):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) WaitForRequestLimit(ctx) error {\n    return s.RequestRateLimit.Wait(ctx)  // Token bucket limiter\n}\n```\n\nExceeding the limit returns `codes.ResourceExhausted`; the proxy backs off and retries.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Performance Considerations\n\n### Debouncing\n- **Problem:** Rapid config changes cause expensive PushContext rebuilds\n- **Solution:** Batch changes within `DebounceAfter` window, apply in one push\n- **Benefit:** Reduces rebuild cost from O(n changes) to O(1)\n\n### Caching\n- **Problem:** Generating the same xDS resource for many proxies is wasteful\n- **Solution:** Cache resources by (proxy, type, names) after first generation\n- **Benefit:** Reduces generation CPU and memory\n\n### Incremental Updates\n- **Problem:** Full pushes recompute all config for all proxies\n- **Solution:** EDS-only pushes reuse PushContext, update only endpoints\n- **Benefit:** 10-100x faster for large deployments with frequent scaling\n\n### Sidecar Scoping\n- **Problem:** Each proxy sees 50+ services, but only needs routes to a few\n- **Solution:** Sidecar resource limits visibility per-proxy\n- **Benefit:** Smaller xDS messages, faster serialization\n\n### Service Index\n- **Problem:** O(n) service lookups in large clusters\n- **Solution:** Pre-index services by namespace, gateway, hostname\n- **Benefit:** O(1) service lookups during generation\n\n---\n\n## 9. Key Source Files Reference\n\n| Component | File | Purpose |\n|-----------|------|---------|\n| **DiscoveryServer** | `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go` | Main server, push orchestration |\n| **ADS/Connection** | `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` | gRPC stream handling, connection lifecycle |\n| **PushContext** | `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` | Config snapshot, indexing |\n| **Push Queue** | `pilot/pkg/xds/push_queue.go` | Concurrent push scheduling |\n| **EDS/Endpoints** | `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go` | Endpoint discovery and updates |\n| **RDS/Routes** | `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go` | Route generation from VirtualServices |\n| **CDS/Clusters** | `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go` | Cluster generation from Services |\n| **LDS/Listeners** | `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go` | Listener generation |\n| **Kubernetes Registry** | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/` | K8s service discovery |\n| **Aggregate Registry** | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/` | Multi-cluster service aggregation |\n| **Config Store** | `pilot/pkg/config/kube/` | Watches Istio CRDs (VirtualService, etc.) |\n| **EndpointIndex** | `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go` | Per-service endpoint storage |\n\n---\n\n## 10. a sophisticated control plane subsystem that bridges the gap between high-level Istio configuration and low-level Envoy proxy control. Its architecture\u2014built around four key components (DiscoveryServer, ADS/Connection, PushContext, ServiceRegistry)\u2014enables:\n\n1. **Real-time configuration distribution** via gRPC streams\n2. **Efficient updates** through debouncing, caching, and incremental pushes\n3. **Consistency** via immutable PushContext snapshots\n4. **Scalability** to support thousands of proxies and hundreds of services\n5. **Extensibility** through custom generators, registries, and policies\n\nThe flow from configuration change to proxy update is carefully orchestrated: changes are debounced, configuration is rebuilt and indexed once, then pushed to all affected proxies concurrently with rate limiting. This design minimizes latency, CPU usage, and memory while ensuring every proxy eventually converges to the desired state.\n",

{
  "content": "# Istio Pilot Discovery Service Architecture\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nIstio Pilot's Discovery Service is the core control plane subsystem that translates high-level Istio service mesh configuration into Envoy-specific xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) resources and pushes them to proxies in real time. It acts as a mediator between:\n\n- **Istio Configuration** \u2014 VirtualServices, DestinationRules, ServiceEntries, Gateways, AuthorizationPolicies, etc.\n- **Service Registries** \u2014 Kubernetes Services, Endpoints, multi-cluster ServiceImports\n- **Envoy Proxies** \u2014 Connected via gRPC/xDS API expecting CDS (Clusters), LDS (Listeners), RDS (Routes), EDS (Endpoints), SDS (Secrets)\n\nThe architecture is organized around four interdependent components: **DiscoveryServer**, **ADS/Connection**, **PushContext**, and **ServiceRegistry**. Together they enable Pilot to efficiently compute and distribute configuration changes to hundreds or thousands of proxies while supporting advanced features like incremental updates, multi-cluster deployments, and custom configuration generators.\n\n---\n\n## 1. DiscoveryServer \u2014 The xDS gRPC Server\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`\n\n### Overview\n\nThe `DiscoveryServer` struct is Pilot's gRPC implementation of Envoy's xDS APIs. It:\n\n- **Implements the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service)** interface \u2014 handles bidirectional gRPC streams with Envoy proxies\n- **Manages proxy connections** \u2014 tracks all currently connected proxies in the `adsClients` map\n- **Orchestrates configuration pushes** \u2014 debounces configuration changes, queues pushes, and rate-limits concurrent operations\n- **Caches xDS resources** \u2014 maintains an in-memory XDS cache to avoid redundant recomputation\n- **Integrates with service registries** \u2014 receives callbacks from Kubernetes controllers and external registries\n\n### Key Responsibilities\n\n#### Connection Management\n```go\ntype DiscoveryServer struct {\n    Env *model.Environment              // Mesh state, owns PushContext\n    adsClients map[string]*Connection    // Active proxy connections\n    adsClientsMutex sync.RWMutex         // Thread-safe access to connections\n\n    // ... other fields\n}\n```\n\nThe server tracks every proxy connection by ID (e.g., `pod-name-1`, `pod-name-2`). When a proxy connects or reconnects, `addCon()` registers it; when it disconnects, `removeCon()` cleans up resources.\n\n#### Debouncing and Throttling\n\nConfiguration changes (from API objects or service registries) don't immediately trigger pushes. Instead, they are debounced:\n\n1. **pushChannel** \u2014 all configuration updates are sent to this buffered channel\n2. **handleUpdates()** \u2014 debounces events with configurable delay (`DebounceAfter`, `debounceMax`)\n3. **pushQueue** \u2014 after debouncing, requests are queued for actual push\n4. **concurrentPushLimit** \u2014 a semaphore limiting concurrent pushes to prevent overwhelming the system\n\n**Debounce behavior:**\n- If events arrive frequently, debouncing delays the push up to `debounceMax` (e.g., 10 seconds)\n- If events stop arriving, a push happens after `DebounceAfter` (default 100ms)\n- This reduces the number of expensive full pushes, especially during cluster-wide operations (e.g., a deployment rolling out)\n\n#### Cache Management\n\nThe `Cache` field is an `XdsCache` instance (typically an in-memory resource cache):\n\n```go\nCache model.XdsCache\n```\n\nWhen a configuration change triggers a full push, the cache can be selectively cleared:\n- For full pushes: `Cache.ClearAll()`\n- For incremental updates: `Cache.Clear(configsUpdated)` \u2014 only clear resources affected by changed configs\n\nThis avoids recomputing Envoy resources that haven't changed.\n\n#### Generators\n\nThe `Generators` map allows customization of xDS resource generation. Different proxy types can use different generators:\n\n```go\nGenerators map[string]model.XdsResourceGenerator\n```\n\nFor example, a custom proxy type might use a special generator for CDS resources, while falling back to the default generator for other types.\n\n#### Lifecycle and Initialization\n\n**Creation:** `NewDiscoveryServer(env, clusterAliases, debugger)` initializes:\n- Connection tracking map\n- Push channel and queue\n- Rate limiters\n- JWT key resolver for JWKS-based authentication\n\n**Registration:** `Register()` registers the server with the gRPC server to handle `StreamAggregatedResources` RPC calls\n\n**Shutdown:** `Shutdown()` closes the JWT resolver and drains the push queue\n\n---\n\n## 2. ADS and the Connection Model\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go`\n\n### Overview\n\nThe Aggregated Discovery Service (ADS) is Envoy's protocol for a single, ordered, bidirectional gRPC stream carrying all xDS resource types. The `Connection` struct wraps a single proxy's stream and coordinates request/response handling.\n\n### Connection Lifecycle\n\n#### Stream Establishment: `Stream()`\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) Stream(stream DiscoveryStream) error {\n    // 1. Check server readiness\n    if !s.IsServerReady() {\n        return \"server not ready\"\n    }\n\n    // 2. Extract peer address\n    peerAddr := extractPeerAddr(stream.Context())\n\n    // 3. Authenticate\n    ids, _ := s.authenticate(ctx)\n\n    // 4. Initialize push context if needed\n    s.globalPushContext().InitContext(s.Env, nil, nil)\n\n    // 5. Create connection and delegate to xds.Stream()\n    con := newConnection(peerAddr, stream)\n    con.ids = ids\n    con.s = s\n    return xds.Stream(con)\n}\n```\n\nThe stream validates preconditions before accepting the connection:\n- **Server readiness:** Pilot must have synced all cache sources (K8s API, config CRDs) before serving\n- **Authentication:** Mutual TLS or SPIFFE identity verification\n- **Rate limiting:** Request limit check via `WaitForRequestLimit()`\n\n#### Connection Initialization: `initConnection()`\n\nOnce the stream is established, the first `DiscoveryRequest` carries the proxy's node metadata (NodeID, version, labels, etc.):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) initConnection(node, con, identities) error {\n    // 1. Parse node metadata\n    proxy, _ := s.initProxyMetadata(node)\n\n    // 2. Apply cluster aliases (multi-cluster)\n    if alias, exists := s.ClusterAliases[proxy.ClusterID]; exists {\n        proxy.ClusterID = alias\n    }\n\n    // 3. Register proxy to receive pushes\n    s.addCon(con.ID(), con)\n\n    // 4. Complete initialization (service targets, sidecar scope, etc.)\n    s.initializeProxy(con)\n}\n```\n\nThis is where Pilot learns the proxy's identity: cluster, namespace, pod labels, workload type (sidecar, ingress, etc.).\n\n### Request Processing: `processRequest()`\n\nEach `DiscoveryRequest` from the proxy specifies:\n- **TypeUrl** \u2014 what resource type is being requested (e.g., `type.googleapis.com/envoy.config.cluster.v3.Cluster`)\n- **ResourceNames** \u2014 optional list of specific resources to subscribe to\n- **VersionInfo** \u2014 the version of resources the proxy last received (for nonce tracking)\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) processRequest(req, con) error {\n    // 1. Debug requests don't trigger watchers\n    if strings.HasPrefix(req.TypeUrl, v3.DebugType) {\n        return s.pushXds(con, ...)\n    }\n\n    // 2. Determine if proxy has unacknowledged resources\n    shouldRespond, delta := xds.ShouldRespond(con.proxy, con.ID(), req)\n    if !shouldRespond {\n        return nil  // No new resources to send\n    }\n\n    // 3. Build push request and send resources for this type\n    request := &model.PushRequest{\n        Full:   true,\n        Push:   con.proxy.LastPushContext,\n        Reason: model.ProxyRequest,\n        Start:  con.proxy.LastPushTime,\n        Delta:  delta,\n    }\n    return s.pushXds(con, con.proxy.GetWatchedResource(req.TypeUrl), request)\n}\n```\n\nThe key insight: Pilot doesn't blindly resend all resources. It uses nonce tracking to understand which versions the proxy has acknowledged, and only sends new or changed resources.\n\n### Push Coordination: `pushConnection()`\n\nWhen a configuration change occurs or Pilot decides to push, `pushConnection()` is called per proxy per push event:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) pushConnection(con *Connection, pushEv *Event) error {\n    req := pushEv.pushRequest\n\n    // 1. Full push: recompute proxy state (service instances, sidecar scope, etc.)\n    if req.Full {\n        s.computeProxyState(con.proxy, req)\n    }\n\n    // 2. Check if proxy needs this push\n    req, needsPush := s.ProxyNeedsPush(con.proxy, req)\n    if !needsPush {\n        return nil  // Skip push if config didn't change for this proxy\n    }\n\n    // 3. Push each resource type in order (CDS \u2192 EDS \u2192 LDS \u2192 RDS \u2192 SDS)\n    wrl := con.watchedResourcesByOrder()\n    for _, w := range wrl {\n        s.pushXds(con, w, req)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Push ordering** (defined in `ads.go:PushOrder`):\n1. **Clusters** \u2014 service definitions\n2. **Endpoints** \u2014 where instances are running\n3. **Listeners** \u2014 inbound/outbound network endpoints\n4. **Routes** \u2014 how to route traffic\n5. **Secrets** \u2014 TLS certificates\n\nThis order ensures Envoy can build dependencies correctly (e.g., routes reference listeners and clusters).\n\n### Broadcast: `StartPush()`\n\nWhen Pilot wants to push to all connected proxies (e.g., after a VirtualService update):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) StartPush(req *model.PushRequest) {\n    req.Start = time.Now()\n    for _, p := range s.AllClients() {\n        s.pushQueue.Enqueue(p, req)\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis enqueues the push request for every proxy. The `pushQueue` (with concurrency limiting) then calls `pushConnection()` concurrently for each proxy.\n\n### Connection Cleanup: `closeConnection()`\n\nWhen a proxy disconnects or Pilot needs to force a disconnect:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) closeConnection(con *Connection) {\n    s.removeCon(con.ID())\n    s.WorkloadEntryController.OnDisconnect(con)\n}\n```\n\nThis removes the proxy from the `adsClients` map and notifies the auto-registration system (for dynamically registered workloads).\n\n---\n\n## 3. PushContext \u2014 Configuration Snapshot and Translation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go`\n\n### Overview\n\n`PushContext` is an **immutable snapshot of all configuration and service data** captured at the moment a push begins. Every push gets its own `PushContext` instance, ensuring consistency: all proxies receiving the same push see the same view of services, routes, policies, etc.\n\n### Structure\n\n```go\ntype PushContext struct {\n    ServiceIndex serviceIndex                      // All services by namespace, gateway, etc.\n    virtualServiceIndex virtualServiceIndex        // VirtualServices by gateway\n    destinationRuleIndex destinationRuleIndex      // DestinationRules by namespace\n    sidecarIndex sidecarIndex                      // Sidecar rules by namespace\n    gatewayIndex gatewayIndex                      // Gateway configs\n\n    envoyFiltersByNamespace map[string][]*EnvoyFilterWrapper\n    wasmPluginsByNamespace map[string][]*WasmPluginWrapper\n\n    AuthnPolicies *AuthenticationPolicies\n    AuthzPolicies *AuthorizationPolicies\n    Telemetry *Telemetries\n    ProxyConfigs *ProxyConfigs\n\n    Mesh *meshconfig.MeshConfig\n    JwtKeyResolver *JwksResolver\n\n    PushVersion string  // Monotonically increasing version ID\n}\n```\n\n### Key Fields and Their Purpose\n\n#### Service Index\nIndexes services for fast lookup during xDS generation:\n- **public** \u2014 services exportable to all namespaces\n- **privateByNamespace** \u2014 namespace-local services\n- **exportedToNamespace** \u2014 services selectively exported to specific namespaces\n- **HostnameAndNamespace** \u2014 all services, keyed by hostname then namespace\n\nThis indexing avoids O(n) lookups during route generation for each proxy.\n\n#### Virtual Service and Destination Rule Indexes\nOrganizes Istio's traffic policies by namespace and gateway:\n- By namespace (private vs. exported)\n- By gateway (Ingress, egress, or mesh internal)\n- By parent-child relationship (for delegated routes)\n\nDuring RDS generation, Pilot looks up the `VirtualService` for a given hostname/gateway and translates it to Envoy `RouteConfiguration`.\n\n#### Config Translation Indexes\n- **sidecarIndex** \u2014 speeds up \"what routes/clusters should this proxy see?\" computations\n- **gatewayIndex** \u2014 indexes gateways for route generation\n- **envoyFilters** \u2014 custom Envoy patches per namespace\n- **wasmPlugins** \u2014 WebAssembly plugins per namespace\n\n### Initialization: `InitContext()`\n\n```go\nfunc (push *PushContext) InitContext(env *model.Environment, oldPushContext, req) {\n    // 1. Build service index from all registries\n    push.buildServiceIndex(env)\n\n    // 2. Build virtual service index\n    push.buildVirtualServiceIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 3. Build destination rule index\n    push.buildDestinationRuleIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 4. Build sidecar index\n    push.buildSidecarIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 5. Build gateway index\n    push.buildGatewayIndex(env.configStore)\n\n    // 6. Collect policies, filters, plugins\n    push.AuthzPolicies = NewAuthorizationPolicies(env)\n    push.AuthnPolicies = NewAuthenticationPolicies(env)\n    // ... etc\n}\n```\n\nThis is the most expensive operation: rebuilding indexes requires iterating over all services, config objects, and policies. That's why debouncing is critical \u2014 we don't want to do this for every small change.\n\n### Config Translation\n\nxDS generators use `PushContext` to look up and translate Istio config to Envoy. Example flow for RDS:\n\n1. **Generator requests routes for a proxy**\n2. **Look up sidecar scope** \u2192 `PushContext.GetProxySidecarScope(proxy)` \u2192 determines which namespaces/services this proxy can access\n3. **For each service hostname the proxy can see:**\n   - `PushContext.VirtualServices(hostname)` \u2192 get VirtualServices for this host\n   - Translate each VS's `http` routes to Envoy `Route` messages\n4. **For each route destination:**\n   - Look up `DestinationRule` \u2192 `PushContext.GetDestinationRule(hostname)`\n   - Extract subset definitions and translate to cluster names\n5. **Return Envoy `RouteConfiguration`**\n\n### Metrics and Error Tracking\n\n`PushContext` tracks push status per proxy:\n\n```go\nProxyStatus map[string]map[string]ProxyPushStatus\n```\n\nAfter generating xDS for a proxy, the status is recorded: did generation succeed? What errors occurred? This data is exposed via the debug API.\n\n### Lifecycle\n\nA new `PushContext` is created **only** on full pushes (when configuration changes):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) Push(req *model.PushRequest) {\n    // Full push: create new context\n    if req.Full {\n        push := s.initPushContext(req, oldContext, version)\n        req.Push = push\n        s.Env.SetPushContext(push)  // Update global context\n    }\n    s.AdsPushAll(req)\n}\n```\n\nIncremental pushes (EDS updates) reuse the current context; they don't rebuild indexes.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Service Registry and Multi-Cluster Support\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/` and `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go`\n\n### Overview\n\nThe service registry is the **data source** for all services and endpoints in the mesh. It translates the underlying platform (Kubernetes, VM, external) into Istio's service model. Changes in the registry (pod scaling, service creation) trigger EDS or CDS pushes via callbacks to `DiscoveryServer`.\n\n### ServiceRegistry Interface\n\nEach cluster or external registry implements the `serviceregistry.Instance` interface:\n\n```go\ntype Instance interface {\n    model.Controller              // Event-driven updates\n    model.ServiceDiscovery        // Service/endpoint queries\n    Provider() provider.ID        // Kubernetes, VM, external, etc.\n    Cluster() cluster.ID          // Which cluster this registry represents\n}\n```\n\n#### ServiceDiscovery Methods\n\n```go\ntype ServiceDiscovery interface {\n    Services() []*Service              // All services in registry\n    GetService(hostname) *Service      // Look up one service\n\n    GetProxyServiceTargets(*Proxy) []ServiceTarget\n    GetProxyWorkloadLabels(*Proxy) labels.Instance\n\n    MCSServices() []MCSServiceInfo\n}\n```\n\n#### Controller Methods\n\n```go\ntype Controller interface {\n    AppendServiceHandler(f ServiceHandler)\n    AppendWorkloadHandler(f func(*WorkloadInstance, Event))\n    Run(stop <-chan struct{})\n    HasSynced() bool\n}\n```\n\nHandlers are called when services or workloads change:\n\n```go\ntype ServiceHandler func(oldService, newService *Service, event Event)\n```\n\n### Kubernetes Implementation\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/controller.go`\n\nThe Kubernetes controller watches:\n- **Services** \u2014 `apps/v1 Service` objects\n- **Endpoints** (or EndpointSlices) \u2014 pod IP and port mappings\n- **Pods** \u2014 workload metadata (labels, node affinity)\n\nWhen an endpoint changes (pod starts/stops), it calls:\n\n```go\ns.SvcUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, event)  // Service-level update\ns.EDSUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints)  // Endpoint-level update\n```\n\n### The Flow: Service Change \u2192 EDS Push\n\n```\nKubernetes Endpoints change (pod scaling)\n    \u2193\nServiceRegistry detects change via watch\n    \u2193\nCalls DiscoveryServer.EDSUpdate()\n    \u2193\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) EDSUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints) {\n    // Update the in-memory endpoint index\n    pushType := s.Env.EndpointIndex.UpdateServiceEndpoints(...)\n\n    // Trigger incremental push if endpoints changed significantly\n    if pushType == IncrementalPush || FullPush {\n        s.ConfigUpdate(&model.PushRequest{\n            Full: pushType == FullPush,\n            ConfigsUpdated: {ServiceEntry: hostname},\n            Reason: EndpointUpdate,\n        })\n    }\n}\n    \u2193\nPushRequest enters pushChannel (debouncing)\n    \u2193\nAfter debounce, Push() is called\n    \u2193\nFor incremental push: reuse PushContext, generate new EDS resources\nFor full push: rebuild PushContext (services might have changed too)\n    \u2193\nStartPush() broadcasts to all proxies\n    \u2193\npushXds() generates Envoy ClusterLoadAssignment (EDS) for each proxy\n```\n\n### Multi-Cluster Support\n\nIstio supports multiple clusters (Kubernetes clusters or VM fleets) via the **aggregate registry** pattern.\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/`\n\n```go\ntype Controller struct {\n    registries []serviceregistry.Instance  // One per cluster/registry\n}\n```\n\nThe aggregate controller:\n1. **Listens to all registered registries** \u2014 each cluster's controller posts events\n2. **Merges service views** \u2014 if multiple clusters have the same service, they're merged into one logical service (keyed by hostname)\n3. **Tracks per-cluster endpoints** \u2014 endpoints include `ShardKey` (cluster + registry source) so Pilot knows which cluster each endpoint came from\n\n#### Multi-Cluster Service Discovery\n\nWhen Pilot looks up a service:\n\n```go\nPushContext.GetAllServices()\n    \u2193\nCalls aggregate.Controller.Services()\n    \u2193\nReturns union of:\n  - Kubernetes services from each cluster\n  - ServiceEntry resources (external services)\n  - ServiceImport resources (MCS - Kubernetes Multi-Cluster Services API)\n```\n\nThe aggregate controller also handles **ServiceImport** (K8s MCS API):\n- When a service is exported from cluster A, a `ServiceImport` is created in cluster B\n- Pilot detects it and synthesizes a cross-cluster endpoint group\n- Routes from cluster B can now point to endpoints in cluster A\n\n### Endpoint Indexing\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go`\n\nEndpoints are stored in `EndpointIndex`, organized by:\n\n```\nServiceName/Namespace/ShardKey (ClusterID + RegistryProvider)\n    \u2193\n[]*IstioEndpoint\n```\n\nEach `IstioEndpoint` carries:\n- Pod IP, port, protocol\n- Labels (used for subset matching)\n- Health status (ready, not ready)\n- Locality (zone, region)\n\nWhen EDS is generated, this index is queried to produce `ClusterLoadAssignment` resources for Envoy.\n\n### Service Entry Integration\n\n`ServiceEntry` resources are Istio's way to declare external services (outside the cluster). They're ingested by the `serviceentry` registry:\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/serviceentry/`\n\n```go\nServiceEntry \u2192 Converted to *model.Service\n    \u2193\nAdded to aggregate service list\n    \u2193\nEndpoints \u2192 Converted to *model.IstioEndpoint\n    \u2193\nAdded to EndpointIndex\n```\n\nThis allows external services to be treated the same as Kubernetes services for routing purposes.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Data Flow: Configuration Change to Envoy Update\n\nThis section traces a complete end-to-end push.\n\n### Scenario: VirtualService Creation\n\n**Event:** User creates a `VirtualService` for `payment.default.svc.cluster.local`, adding traffic splitting and retries.\n\n```\n1. Kubernetes API receives VirtualService\n   \u2514\u2500\u2192 Pilot's config store watchers are notified\n\n2. Pilot's config store (kube/config/) receives add event\n   \u2514\u2500\u2192 Calls ConfigUpdate() with ConfigKey{VirtualService, payment, default}\n\n3. ConfigUpdate() is called on DiscoveryServer:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) ConfigUpdate(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       inboundConfigUpdates.Increment()\n       s.pushChannel <- req   // Send to debouncer\n   }\n\n4. handleUpdates() debounces in separate goroutine:\n\n   - Starts debounce timer\n   - If more events arrive, resets timer\n   - Once quiet period (`DebounceAfter`) is reached, calls Push()\n\n5. Push() initiates full push (VirtualService affects routes):\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) Push(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       // Create new PushContext\n       push := s.initPushContext(req, oldContext, versionID)\n       req.Push = push\n       s.Env.SetPushContext(push)\n\n       // Re-index all VirtualServices (rebuilds virtualServiceIndex)\n       push.buildVirtualServiceIndex(s.Env.ConfigStore)\n\n       // Notify all proxies\n       s.AdsPushAll(req)\n   }\n\n6. AdsPushAll() queues push for all proxies:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) AdsPushAll(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       s.StartPush(req)\n   }\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) StartPush(req *model.PushRequest) {\n       for _, proxy := range s.AllClients() {\n           s.pushQueue.Enqueue(proxy, req)\n       }\n   }\n\n7. pushQueue worker processes push (with concurrency limit):\n\n   - Limits to features.PushThrottle concurrent pushes\n   - Calls pushConnection(proxy, event) for each proxy\n\n8. pushConnection() determines what to send:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) pushConnection(con, pushEv) {\n       if pushEv.Full {\n           // Recompute sidecar scope, service targets\n           s.computeProxyState(con.proxy, pushEv)\n       }\n\n       if !s.ProxyNeedsPush(con.proxy, pushEv) {\n           return  // Skip if VirtualService doesn't affect this proxy\n       }\n\n       // Push each resource in order\n       for _, w := range con.watchedResourcesByOrder() {\n           s.pushXds(con, w, pushEv)\n       }\n   }\n\n9. pushXds() delegates to the generator:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) pushXds(con, w, req) {\n       gen := s.findGenerator(w.TypeUrl, con)\n       resources, _, _ := gen.Generate(con.proxy, w, req)\n       // Send resources to proxy via gRPC\n   }\n\n10. RDS Generator produces RouteConfiguration:\n\n    func (g *RdsGenerator) Generate(proxy, w, pushContext) {\n        // Look up VirtualService for each watched hostname\n        vs := pushContext.VirtualServices(hostname)\n\n        // Translate VirtualService to Envoy Route\n        routes := translateVirtualService(vs, pushContext, proxy)\n\n        // Return Envoy RouteConfiguration\n        return routes\n    }\n\n11. Proxy receives RouteConfiguration:\n\n    - Proxy deserializes and validates config\n    - Updates its internal route table\n    - Begins using new routes for traffic\n    - Sends ACK nonce in next request\n```\n\n### Scenario: Pod Scaling (EDS Update)\n\n**Event:** Kubernetes deployment scales from 2 to 5 replicas, creating 3 new pods.\n\n```\n1. Kubernetes detects new pods, updates Endpoints resource\n\n2. Kubernetes controller in Istio watches Endpoints:\n\n   func (c *Controller) onEndpointsUpdate(oldEps, newEps) {\n       // Extract pod IPs, ports, labels\n       c.updateEndpointShards(newEps)\n\n       // Convert to IstioEndpoint\n       istioEps := convertToIstioEndpoints(newEps)\n\n       // Notify xDS\n       s.EDSUpdate(shardKey, hostname, namespace, istioEps)\n   }\n\n3. EDSUpdate() queues incremental push:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) EDSUpdate(shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints) {\n       // Update in-memory endpoint index\n       pushType := s.Env.EndpointIndex.UpdateServiceEndpoints(\n           shard, hostname, namespace, endpoints, triggerPush=true)\n\n       if pushType == IncrementalPush {\n           s.ConfigUpdate(&model.PushRequest{\n               Full: false,  // Incremental!\n               ConfigsUpdated: {ServiceEntry: hostname},\n               Reason: EndpointUpdate,\n           })\n       }\n   }\n\n4. ConfigUpdate() sends to pushChannel (debounced)\n\n5. handleUpdates() debounces, but since Full=false:\n\n   if !opts.enableEDSDebounce && !r.Full {\n       // EDS pushes happen immediately, don't wait for debounce\n       go pushFn(r)\n   }\n\n6. Push() with Full=false skips PushContext rebuild:\n\n   func (s *DiscoveryServer) Push(req) {\n       if !req.Full {\n           // Reuse existing PushContext\n           req.Push = s.globalPushContext()\n           s.AdsPushAll(req)\n           return\n       }\n       // ... full push logic ...\n   }\n\n7. AdsPushAll() queues for all proxies (same as before)\n\n8. pushConnection() runs for each proxy:\n\n   - No full proxy state recompute (Full=false)\n   - Still checks ProxyNeedsPush (does this proxy care about this service?)\n   - Pushes resources in order\n\n9. EDS Generator produces ClusterLoadAssignment:\n\n   func (g *EdsGenerator) Generate(proxy, w, pushContext) {\n       // Look up endpoint index for service\n       endpoints := pushContext.Endpoints(hostname)\n\n       // Build Envoy ClusterLoadAssignment with new pod IPs\n       return buildClusterLoadAssignment(endpoints)\n   }\n\n10. Proxy receives ClusterLoadAssignment:\n\n    - Adds 3 new endpoints to its load balancer\n    - Begins health checking new pods\n    - Distributes traffic to all 5 pods\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points\n\nIstio provides several mechanisms for users to extend the discovery system:\n\n### 1. Custom Resource Generators\n\n**Source:** `pilot/pkg/model/context.go` and `pilot/pkg/xds/xdsgen.go`\n\nRegister a custom generator via the Generators map:\n\n```go\ntype MyGenerator struct {\n    Server *DiscoveryServer\n}\n\nfunc (g *MyGenerator) Generate(proxy, w, pushContext) (resources, logData, error) {\n    // Custom logic to generate Envoy resources\n    return envoyProtos, debug, nil\n}\n\n// Register\ndiscovery.Generators[\"/my-typeurl\"] = &MyGenerator{discovery}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Custom xDS types for specialized proxies\n- Vendor-specific resource generation\n- Testing/debugging utilities\n\n### 2. External Service Registries\n\nImplement `serviceregistry.Instance`:\n\n```go\ntype CustomRegistry struct {\n    // ... service store, mutex, etc ...\n}\n\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) Services() []*Service { ... }\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) GetService(host) *Service { ... }\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) AppendServiceHandler(f ServiceHandler) { ... }\nfunc (r *CustomRegistry) Run(stop <-chan struct{}) { ... }\n```\n\nRegister with the aggregate controller:\n\n```go\naggregateController.AddRegistry(customRegistry)\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Consul service discovery\n- Eureka, Nacos, or other registries\n- Internal CMDB or metadata systems\n\n### 3. Custom PushContext Builders\n\nOverride how `PushContext` indexes services and policies. Extend `PushContext.InitContext()`:\n\n```go\nfunc (p *PushContext) InitContext(env, oldContext, req) {\n    // ... default indexing ...\n\n    // Custom indexing\n    p.customIndex = buildCustomIndex(env)\n}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Performance optimization for large deployments\n- Custom service grouping logic\n- Domain-specific policies\n\n### 4. Telemetry and Metrics\n\nHook into push lifecycle:\n\n```go\n// Before push\noldPushContext.OnConfigChange()\n\n// During push\naddMetric(metric, node, msg)\n\n// After push\nproxiesConvergeDelay.Record(duration)\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Monitoring push latency and errors\n- Tracking proxy convergence time\n- Detecting configuration churn\n\n### 5. Configuration Update Filtering\n\nOverride `ProxyNeedsPush()`:\n\n```go\nfunc customProxyNeedsPush(proxy *Proxy, req *PushRequest) (*PushRequest, bool) {\n    // Decide: does this proxy care about this change?\n    if req.ConfigsUpdated.Has(gatewayCRD) && !proxy.IsGateway {\n        return req, false  // Skip push\n    }\n    return req, true  // Send push\n}\n\ndiscovery.ProxyNeedsPush = customProxyNeedsPush\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Minimize redundant pushes for large clusters\n- Optimize for deployments with many isolated services\n\n### 6. Security: Custom Authenticators and Authorizers\n\nRegister custom authenticators before stream establishment:\n\n```go\ndiscovery.Authenticators = append(discovery.Authenticators, customAuth)\n```\n\nImplement:\n\n```go\ntype CustomAuth struct {}\nfunc (a *CustomAuth) Authenticate(ctx) ([]string, error) {\n    // Extract identity from mTLS cert, JWT token, etc.\n    return identities, nil\n}\n```\n\nUse cases:\n- Custom mTLS certificate validation\n- External identity provider integration\n- Audit logging\n\n---\n\n## 7. Error Handling\n\n### Configuration Validation\n\nInvalid Istio configuration (bad `VirtualService`, etc.) is detected during indexing:\n\n- **Type mismatch** \u2014 port not found in destination service\n- **Circular references** \u2014 delegation loops in routes\n- **Policy conflicts** \u2014 ambiguous DestinationRules\n\n**Action:** Log warning, index the config as-is, let xDS generators handle or skip.\n\n### Push Failures\n\nIf generating xDS for a proxy fails:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) pushXds(con, w, req) {\n    res, _, err := gen.Generate(con.proxy, w, req)\n    if err != nil {\n        // Record error in proxy status\n        pushContext.AddMetric(metrics.PushContextErrors, ..., err.String())\n        // Log and skip this resource type\n        return err\n    }\n}\n```\n\nProxy status is recorded in `PushContext.ProxyStatus`:\n\n```\nProxyStatus[\"generation_error\"][\"proxy-id\"] = {\n    Error: \"failed to generate CDS: unknown service\",\n}\n```\n\nExposed via debug API (`/debug/push_context`) so operators can investigate.\n\n### Network Failures\n\nIf sending the xDS response fails:\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) pushXds(con, w, req) {\n    // ... generate resources ...\n\n    if err := con.stream.Send(response); err != nil {\n        // Proxy disconnected or network error\n        s.closeConnection(con)\n        return err\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe proxy is removed from `adsClients`; it will reconnect and re-request resources.\n\n### Cache Staleness\n\nThe XDS cache maps resources by content hash and timestamp:\n\n```\nCacheKey: {Proxy.ID, TypeUrl, ResourceNames}\nValue: {Resources, Timestamp}\n```\n\nWhen a new `PushContext` is created, the timestamp is updated. Old cache entries are considered stale and evicted.\n\n### Rate Limiting\n\nIf too many proxies reconnect simultaneously (thundering herd):\n\n```go\nfunc (s *DiscoveryServer) WaitForRequestLimit(ctx) error {\n    return s.RequestRateLimit.Wait(ctx)  // Token bucket limiter\n}\n```\n\nExceeding the limit returns `codes.ResourceExhausted`; the proxy backs off and retries.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Performance Considerations\n\n### Debouncing\n- **Problem:** Rapid config changes cause expensive PushContext rebuilds\n- **Solution:** Batch changes within `DebounceAfter` window, apply in one push\n- **Benefit:** Reduces rebuild cost from O(n changes) to O(1)\n\n### Caching\n- **Problem:** Generating the same xDS resource for many proxies is wasteful\n- **Solution:** Cache resources by (proxy, type, names) after first generation\n- **Benefit:** Reduces generation CPU and memory\n\n### Incremental Updates\n- **Problem:** Full pushes recompute all config for all proxies\n- **Solution:** EDS-only pushes reuse PushContext, update only endpoints\n- **Benefit:** 10-100x faster for large deployments with frequent scaling\n\n### Sidecar Scoping\n- **Problem:** Each proxy sees 50+ services, but only needs routes to a few\n- **Solution:** Sidecar resource limits visibility per-proxy\n- **Benefit:** Smaller xDS messages, faster serialization\n\n### Service Index\n- **Problem:** O(n) service lookups in large clusters\n- **Solution:** Pre-index services by namespace, gateway, hostname\n- **Benefit:** O(1) service lookups during generation\n\n---\n\n## 9. Key Source Files Reference\n\n| Component | File | Purpose |\n|-----------|------|---------|\n| **DiscoveryServer** | `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go` | Main server, push orchestration |\n| **ADS/Connection** | `pilot/pkg/xds/ads.go` | gRPC stream handling, connection lifecycle |\n| **PushContext** | `pilot/pkg/model/push_context.go` | Config snapshot, indexing |\n| **Push Queue** | `pilot/pkg/xds/push_queue.go` | Concurrent push scheduling |\n| **EDS/Endpoints** | `pilot/pkg/xds/eds.go` | Endpoint discovery and updates |\n| **RDS/Routes** | `pilot/pkg/xds/rds.go` | Route generation from VirtualServices |\n| **CDS/Clusters** | `pilot/pkg/xds/cds.go` | Cluster generation from Services |\n| **LDS/Listeners** | `pilot/pkg/xds/lds.go` | Listener generation |\n| **Kubernetes Registry** | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/kube/controller/` | K8s service discovery |\n| **Aggregate Registry** | `pilot/pkg/serviceregistry/aggregate/` | Multi-cluster service aggregation |\n| **Config Store** | `pilot/pkg/config/kube/` | Watches Istio CRDs (VirtualService, etc.) |\n| **EndpointIndex** | `pilot/pkg/model/endpointshards.go` | Per-service endpoint storage |\n\n---\n\n## 10. Architecture a sophisticated control plane subsystem that bridges the gap between high-level Istio configuration and low-level Envoy proxy control. Its architecture\u2014built around four key components (DiscoveryServer, ADS/Connection, PushContext, ServiceRegistry)\u2014enables:\n\n1. **Real-time configuration distribution** via gRPC streams\n2. **Efficient updates** through debouncing, caching, and incremental pushes\n3. **Consistency** via immutable PushContext snapshots\n4. **Scalability** to support thousands of proxies and hundreds of services\n5. **Extensibility** through custom generators, registries, and policies\n\nThe flow from configuration change to proxy update is carefully orchestrated: changes are debounced, configuration is rebuilt and indexed once, then pushed to all affected proxies concurrently with rate limiting. This design minimizes latency, CPU usage, and memory while ensuring every proxy eventually converges to the desired state.\n",

1. WRITE /workspace/documentation.md
# Istio Pilot Discovery Service Architecture

## Executive Summary

Istio Pilot's Discovery Service is the core control plane subsystem that translates high-level Istio service mesh configuration into Envoy-specific xDS (Envoy Discovery Service) resources and pushes them to proxies in real time. It acts as a mediator between:

- **Istio Configuration** — VirtualServices, DestinationRules, ServiceEntries, Gateways, AuthorizationPolicies, etc.
- **Service Registries** — Kubernetes Services, Endpoints, multi-cluster ServiceImports
- **Envoy Proxies** — Connected via gRPC/xDS API expecting CDS (Clusters), LDS (Listeners), RDS (Routes), EDS (Endpoints), SDS (Secrets)

The architecture is organized around four interdependent components: **DiscoveryServer**, **ADS/Connection**, **PushContext**, and **ServiceRegistry**. Together they enable Pilot to efficiently compute and distribute configuration changes to hundreds or thousands of proxies while supporting advanced features like incremental updates, multi-cluster deployments, and custom configuration generators.

---

## 1. DiscoveryServer — The xDS gRPC Server

**Source:** `pilot/pkg/xds/discovery.go`

### Overview

The `DiscoveryServer` struct is Pilot's gRPC implementation of Envoy's xDS APIs. It:

- **Implements the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service)** interface — handles bidirectional gRPC streams with Envoy proxies
- **Manages proxy connections** — tracks all currently connected proxies in the `adsClients` map
- **Orchestrates configuration pushes** — debounces configuration changes, queues pushes, and rate-limits concurrent operations
- **Caches xDS resources** — maintains an in-memory XDS cache to avoid redundant recomputation
- **Integrates with service registries** — receives callbacks from Kubernetes controllers and
... (truncated)
